window['backfillParam']['pl_tmodn']
=
3;








}






function
google_ad_request_done(google_ads)
{




window['google_ads']
=
google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Busta_Rhymes';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"busta,_,rhymes,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Trevor
Tahiem
Smith,
Jr.</b>,
(born
May
20,
1972),<sup
id="cite_ref-ALLMUSIC_2-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ALLMUSIC-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
better
known
by
his
stage
name
<b>Busta
Rhymes</b>,
is
an
American
rapper,
producer,
and
actor
from
<a
href="/wiki/Brooklyn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>.
<a
href="/wiki/Chuck_D?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chuck
D">Chuck
D</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Public_Enemy_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Public
Enemy
(band)"
class="mw-redirect">Public
Enemy</a>
gave
him
the
<a
href="/wiki/Moniker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Moniker"
class="mw-redirect">moniker</a>
Busta
Rhymes,
after
<a
href="/wiki/National_Football_League?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="National
Football
League">NFL</a>
wide
receiver
<a
href="/wiki/Buster_Rhymes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buster
Rhymes">George
&quot;Buster&quot;
Rhymes</a>.
Early
in
his
career,
he
was
known
for
his
wild
style
and
fashion,
and
today
is
best
known
for
his
intricate
rapping
technique,
which
involves
rapping
at
a
fast
rate
with
lots
of
<a
href="/wiki/Internal_rhyme?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Internal
rhyme">internal
rhyme</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Half_rhyme?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Half
rhyme">half
rhyme</a>,
and
to
date
has
received
eleven
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy</a>
nominations
for
his
musical
work.</p>








<p><a
href="/wiki/About.com?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="About.com">About.com</a>
included
him
on
its
list
of
the
50
Greatest
MCs
of
Our
Time
(1987–2007),<sup
id="cite_ref-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
while
Steve
Huey
of
<a
href="/wiki/Allmusic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Allmusic"
class="mw-redirect">Allmusic</a>
called
him
one
of
the
best
and
most
prolific
rappers
of
the
1990s.<sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2012,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Source_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Source
(magazine)">The
Source</a></i>
placed
him
on
their
list
of
the
Top
50
Lyricists
of
All
Time.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(June
2013)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
<a
href="/wiki/MTV?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV">MTV</a>
has
called
him
&quot;one
of
hip-hop's
greatest
visual
artists.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Busta
Rhymes
was
both
a
member
of
<a
href="/wiki/Leaders_of_the_New_School?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Leaders
of
the
New
School">Leaders
of
the
New
School</a>
and
a
founding
member
of
the
record
label
<a
href="/wiki/Conglomerate_(record_label)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Conglomerate
(record
label)">Conglomerate</a>
(founded
as
Flipmode
Entertainment)
and
production
crew
<a
href="/wiki/The_Conglomerate_(American_group)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Conglomerate
(American
group)">The
Conglomerate</a>
(formerly
Flipmode
Squad).
In
November
2011,
Busta
Rhymes
signed
a
deal
with
<a
href="/wiki/Cash_Money_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cash
Money
Records">Cash
Money
Records</a>.
He
has
so
far
released
eight
studio
albums,
with
the
first
being
the
1995
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">platinum-selling</a>
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Coming?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Coming">The
Coming</a></i>.
His
list
of
<a
href="/wiki/Hit_single?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hit
single">hit
singles</a>
include
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Woo_Hah!!_Got_You_All_in_Check?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Woo
Hah!!
Got
You
All
in
Check">Woo
Hah!!
Got
You
All
in
Check</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Dangerous_(Busta_Rhymes_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dangerous
(Busta
Rhymes
song)">Dangerous</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Turn_It_Up_(Remix)/Fire_It_Up?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Turn
It
Up
(Remix)/Fire
It
Up">Turn
It
Up
(Remix)/Fire
It
Up</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/What%27s_It_Gonna_Be%3F!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="What's
It
Gonna
Be?!">What's
It
Gonna
Be?!</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Pass_the_Courvoisier,_Part_II?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pass
the
Courvoisier,
Part
II">Pass
the
Courvoisier,
Part
II</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Know_What_You_Want?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Know
What
You
Want">I
Know
What
You
Want</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Touch_It?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Touch
It">Touch
It</a>&quot;,
among
several
others.
He
is
set
to
release
his
Cash
Money
debut,
<i><a
href="/wiki/E.L.E.2_(Extinction_Level_Event_2)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="E.L.E.2
(Extinction
Level
Event
2)">E.L.E.2
(Extinction
Level
Event
2)</a></i>,
in
2014,
which
will
be
a
sequel
to
his
1998
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/E.L.E._(Extinction_Level_Event):_The_Final_World_Front?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="E.L.E.
(Extinction
Level
Event):
The
Final
World
Front">E.L.E.
(Extinction
Level
Event):
The
Final
World
Front</a></i>.</p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_life">Early
life</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
Early
life">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Busta
Rhymes
was
born
Trevor
Tahiem
Smith,
Jr.,
in
<a
href="/wiki/Brooklyn,_New_York?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brooklyn,
New
York"
class="mw-redirect">Brooklyn,
New
York</a>,
on
May
20,
1972.<sup
id="cite_ref-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
age
12,
he
moved
to
<a
href="/wiki/Uniondale,_New_York?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Uniondale,
New
York">Uniondale</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Long_Island?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Long
Island">Long
Island</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
later
attended
<a
href="/wiki/Uniondale_High_School?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Uniondale
High
School">Uniondale
High
School</a>,
graduating
in
1991.<sup
id="cite_ref-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
Smith
attended
<a
href="/wiki/George_Westinghouse_Career_and_Technical_Education_High_School?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Westinghouse
Career
and
Technical
Education
High
School">George
Westinghouse
Career
and
Technical
Education
High
School</a>,
alongside
<a
href="/wiki/Jay-Z?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/DMX_(rapper)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="DMX
(rapper)">DMX</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Notorious
B.I.G.">The
Notorious
B.I.G.</a><sup
id="cite_ref-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Music_career">Music
career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Music
career">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1989.E2.80.931993:_Leaders_of_the_New_School_and_rising_popularity">1989–1993:
Leaders
of
the
New
School
and
rising
popularity</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
1989–1993:
Leaders
of
the
New
School
and
rising
popularity">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
1989,
Smith,
alongside
fellow
<a
href="/wiki/New_York?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York">New
York</a>
natives
Charlie
Brown
(born
Bryan
Higgins),
Dinco
D
(born
James
Jackson)
and
Cut
Monitor
Milo
(born
Sheldon
Scott),
formed
the
<a
href="/wiki/East_Coast_hip_hop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="East
Coast
hip
hop">East
Coast
hip
hop</a>
group
<a
href="/wiki/Leaders_of_the_New_School?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Leaders
of
the
New
School">Leaders
of
the
New
School</a>.
The
group's
big
break
was
when
they
became
an
<a
href="/wiki/Opening_act?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Opening
act">opening
act</a>
for
fellow
<a
href="/wiki/Long_Island?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Long
Island">Long
Island</a>
hip
hop
group
<a
href="/wiki/Public_Enemy_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Public
Enemy
(band)"
class="mw-redirect">Public
Enemy</a>.
Public
Enemy's
<a
href="/wiki/Chuck_D?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chuck
D">Chuck
D</a>
gave
Busta
Rhymes
and
Charlie
Brown
their
respective
<a
href="/wiki/Stage_name?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stage
name">stage
names</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-ALLMUSIC_2-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ALLMUSIC-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
Leaders
of
the
New
School<sup
id="cite_ref-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
began
recording
in
1989
and
released
their
debut
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/A_Future_Without_a_Past...?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Future
Without
a
Past...">A
Future
Without
a
Past...</a></i>
in
1991
on
<a
href="/wiki/Elektra_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elektra
Records">Elektra
Records</a>.
In
early
1992,
the
group
appeared
on
<a
href="/wiki/A_Tribe_Called_Quest?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Tribe
Called
Quest">A
Tribe
Called
Quest</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/Posse_cut?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Posse
cut">posse
cut</a>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Scenario_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scenario
(song)">Scenario</a>,&quot;
in
which
Busta
Rhymes's
climactic
verse
propelled
him
into
the
cultural
consciousness.<sup
id="cite_ref-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1993,
they
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/T.I.M.E._(The_Inner_Mind%27s_Eye)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="T.I.M.E.
(The
Inner
Mind's
Eye)">T.I.M.E.
(The
Inner
Mind's
Eye)</a></i>.
Soon
after,
however,
internal
problems
arose
because
of
Busta
Rhymes's
increasing
popularity,
and
the
group
broke
up
on
the
set
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Yo!_MTV_Raps?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yo!
MTV
Raps">Yo!
MTV
Raps</a></i>.</p>








<p>In
the
years
between
1992
and
1995,
Rhymes
began
making
<a
href="/wiki/Guest_appearance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guest
appearance">guest
appearances</a>
on
songs
by
several
artists
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Big_Daddy_Kane?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Big
Daddy
Kane">Big
Daddy
Kane</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Another_Bad_Creation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Another
Bad
Creation">Another
Bad
Creation</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Notorious
B.I.G.">The
Notorious
B.I.G.</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Brand_Nubian?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brand
Nubian">Brand
Nubian</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/A_Tribe_Called_Quest?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Tribe
Called
Quest">A
Tribe
Called
Quest</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/KRS-One?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="KRS-One">KRS-One</a>,
as
well
on
the
interludes
to
<a
href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mary
J.
Blige">Mary
J.
Blige</a>'s
debut
<i><a
href="/wiki/What%27s_the_411%3F?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="What's
the
411?">What's
the
411?</a></i>
(1992)
and
<a
href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Contemporary
R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>
trio
<a
href="/wiki/TLC_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="TLC
(band)"
class="mw-redirect">TLC</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">Diamond-certified</a>
second
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/CrazySexyCool?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="CrazySexyCool">CrazySexyCool</a></i>
(1994).
He
also
appeared
on
the
album
jacket
of
fellow
hip-hop
group
<a
href="/wiki/A_Tribe_Called_Quest?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Tribe
Called
Quest">A
Tribe
Called
Quest</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/Midnight_Marauders?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Midnight
Marauders">Midnight
Marauders</a></i>,
with
a
host
of
other
fellow
hip-hop
pioneers.
In
1993,
he
appeared
in
a
cameo
role
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/Yo!_MTV_Raps?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yo!
MTV
Raps">Yo!
MTV
Raps'</a></i>
hosts
<a
href="/wiki/Doctor_Dr%C3%A9?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Doctor
Dr&eacute;">Doctor
Dr&eacute;</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Ed_Lover?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ed
Lover">Ed
Lover</a>'s
film,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Who%27s_the_Man%3F?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Who's
the
Man?">Who's
the
Man?</a></i>
(1993)
and
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/HBO?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="HBO">HBO
film</a>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Strapped?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Strapped">Strapped</a></i>
(directed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Forest_Whitaker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Forest
Whitaker">Forest
Whitaker</a>)
and
co-starred
alongside
<a
href="/wiki/Ice_Cube?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ice
Cube">Ice
Cube</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Omar_Epps?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Omar
Epps">Omar
Epps</a>
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/John_Singleton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Singleton">John
Singleton</a>
film,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Higher_Learning_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Higher
Learning
(film)"
class="mw-redirect">Higher
Learning</a></i>
(which
was
in
post-production
until
it
was
released
in
1995).
The
following
year,
he
teamed
up
with
<a
href="/wiki/Sean_Combs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sean
Combs">Puff
Daddy</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/LL_Cool_J?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="LL
Cool
J">LL
Cool
J</a>,
future
Flipmode
Squad
member
<a
href="/wiki/Rampage_(rapper)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rampage
(rapper)">Rampage</a>
and
former
classmate
<a
href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Notorious
B.I.G.">The
Notorious
B.I.G.</a>,
on
a
remix
to
<a
href="/wiki/Craig_Mack?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Craig
Mack">Craig
Mack</a>'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Flava_In_Ya_Ear?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Flava
In
Ya
Ear"
class="mw-redirect">Flava
In
Ya
Ear</a>&quot;,
soon
after
he
would
team
up
again
with
The
Notorious
B.I.G.
among
a
plethora
of
rappers
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Bone_Thugs-n-Harmony?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bone
Thugs-n-Harmony">Bone
Thugs-n-Harmony</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Coolio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Coolio">Coolio</a>
on
the
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Points?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Points">The
Points</a>&quot;
which
appeared
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Panther_(soundtrack)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Panther
(soundtrack)">soundtrack</a>
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/1995_in_film?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="1995
in
film">1995</a>
film,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Panther_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Panther
(film)">Panther</a></i>.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1995.E2.80.931997:_The_Coming_and_When_Disaster_Strikes">1995–1997:
<i>The
Coming</i>
and
<i>When
Disaster
Strikes</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
1995–1997:
The
Coming
and
When
Disaster
Strikes">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
the
summer
of
1995,
Busta
Rhymes
began
working
on
his
solo
debut
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Coming?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Coming">The
Coming</a></i>,
and
a
month
after
recording
the
album,
he
released
it
in
March
1996.
A
month
before
the
album
was
released,
he
broke
out
with
a
hit
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Woo_Hah!!_Got_You_All_in_Check?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Woo
Hah!!
Got
You
All
in
Check">Woo
Hah!!
Got
You
All
in
Check</a>&quot;.
Later,
he
started
work
on
his
second
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/When_Disaster_Strikes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="When
Disaster
Strikes"
class="mw-redirect">When
Disaster
Strikes</a></i>,
which
would
not
be
released
until
September
1997.
It
produced
the
hit
singles
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Put_Your_Hands_Where_My_Eyes_Could_See?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Put
Your
Hands
Where
My
Eyes
Could
See">Put
Your
Hands
Where
My
Eyes
Could
See</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Turn_It_Up_(Remix)/Fire_It_Up?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Turn
It
Up
(Remix)/Fire
It
Up">Fire
It
Up</a>&quot;.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1998.E2.80.931999:_Extinction_Level_Event_.28Final_World_Front.29">1998–1999:
<i>Extinction
Level
Event
(Final
World
Front)</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
1998–1999:
Extinction
Level
Event
(Final
World
Front)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
1998,
Busta
Rhymes
recorded
<i><a
href="/wiki/Extinction_Level_Event_(Final_World_Front)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Extinction
Level
Event
(Final
World
Front)"
class="mw-redirect">Extinction
Level
Event
(Final
World
Front)</a></i>.
Its
lead
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Gimme_Some_More?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gimme
Some
More">Gimme
Some
More</a>&quot;
—
which
sampled
<a
href="/wiki/Bernard_Herrmann?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bernard
Herrmann">Bernard
Herrmann</a>'s
theme
from
<i><a
href="/wiki/Psycho_(1960_film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Psycho
(1960
film)">Psycho</a></i>
—
reached
number
6
in
the
UK
singles
chart
in
January
1999.
Busta
Rhymes
enjoyed
further
transatlantic
success
in
April,
when
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/What%27s_It_Gonna_Be%3F!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="What's
It
Gonna
Be?!">What's
It
Gonna
Be?!</a>&quot;,
featuring
<a
href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Janet
Jackson">Janet
Jackson</a>,
reached
the
US
and
UK
Top
11.
The
album
received
prominent
notice
for
featuring
the
fastest
<a
href="/wiki/Rapping?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rapping">rapping</a>
Busta
Rhymes
has
ever
performed,
particularly
on
a
song
called
&quot;Iz
They
Wildin
Wit
Us?&quot;,
featuring
a
guest
appearance
by
<a
href="/wiki/Mystikal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mystikal">Mystikal</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-ALLMUSIC_2-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ALLMUSIC-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>That
same
year,
the
Flipmode
Squad
released
their
group
album,
and
from
there,
they
continued
to
collaborate.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2000.E2.80.932004:_J.2FArista.2FBMG_era">2000–2004:
J/Arista/BMG
era</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"

era">edit</a>]</span></h3>

Busta
Rhymes
performing
in
2006









</div>

<dl>









<dt>









<i>Anarchy</i>
and










<i>Genesis</i>
(2000–2001)








</dt>








</dl>








<p>In
2000,
Busta
Rhymes
recorded
his
final
album
for
Elektra,
entitled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Anarchy_(Busta_Rhymes_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Anarchy
(Busta
Rhymes
album)">Anarchy</a></i>.
After
Busta
signed
to
<a
href="/wiki/J_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="J
Records">J
Records</a>,
a
label
started
by
the
then
recently
ousted
<a
href="/wiki/Arista_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Arista
Records">Arista
Records</a>
chief
and
founder
<a
href="/wiki/Clive_Davis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Clive
Davis">Clive
Davis</a>,
he
released
a
greatest
hits
collection
<i><a
href="/wiki/Total_Devastation:_The_Best_of_Busta_Rhymes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Total
Devastation:
The
Best
of
Busta
Rhymes">Total
Devastation:
The
Best
of
Busta
Rhymes</a></i>,
alongside
a
new
album
of
original
work.
Continuing
the
<a
href="/wiki/Bible?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bible">Biblical</a>
theme
of
his
previous
albums,
he
titled
his
record
<i><a
href="/wiki/Genesis_(Busta_Rhymes_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Genesis
(Busta
Rhymes
album)">Genesis</a></i>.
The
album
featured
collaborations
with
<a
href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mary
J.
Blige">Mary
J.
Blige</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/P._Diddy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="P.
Diddy"
class="mw-redirect">P.
Diddy</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Kelis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kelis">Kelis</a>,
and
others.
Genesis
was
powered
by
the
hit
single
with
Kelis,
&quot;What
It
Is&quot;,
and
his
solo
single
released
in
November
2001,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Break_Ya_Neck?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Break
Ya
Neck">Break
Ya
Neck</a>&quot;.
The
final
single
was
the
summer
smash
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Pass_the_Courvoisier,_Part_II?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pass
the
Courvoisier,
Part
II">Pass
the
Courvoisier,
Part
II</a>&quot;,
which
featured
<a
href="/wiki/Pharrell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pharrell"
class="mw-redirect">Pharrell</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/P._Diddy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="P.
Diddy"
class="mw-redirect">P.
Diddy</a>.
Despite
the
success
of
the
two
singles,
this
album
did
not
sell
as
well
as
previous
releases.
Fellow
Flipmode
members
were
featured,
but
minor
changes
in
the
roster
were
noted.</p>








<dl>









<dt>









<i>It
Aint
Safe
No
More</i>
(2002–2004)








</dt>








</dl>








<p>In
2002,
Busta
Rhymes
released
his
sixth
studio
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/It_Ain%27t_Safe_No_More?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="It
Ain't
Safe
No
More"
class="mw-redirect">It
Ain't
Safe
No
More</a></i>.
The
album
was
moderately
successful,
with
a
hit
song
featuring
<a
href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mariah
Carey">Mariah
Carey</a>
and
the
Flipmode
Squadtitled
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Know_What_You_Want?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Know
What
You
Want">I
Know
What
You
Want</a>&quot;.
Another
hit
single
was
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Make_It_Clap?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Make
It
Clap">Make
It
Clap</a>&quot;,
featuring
Spliff
Starr.
The
<a
href="/wiki/Remix?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Remix">remix</a>
of
&quot;Make
It
Clap&quot;,
features
<a
href="/wiki/Sean_Paul?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sean
Paul">Sean
Paul</a>.
After
its
release,
Busta
Rhymes
left
<a
href="/wiki/J_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="J
Records">J
Records</a>.
In
2004,
he
signed
with
American
record
producer
and
record
executive
<a
href="/wiki/Dr._Dre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dr.
Dre">Dr.
Dre</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aftermath
Entertainment">Aftermath
Entertainment</a>,
through
<a
href="/wiki/Interscope_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Interscope
Records">Interscope
Records</a>.
Consequently,
upon
changing
label,
a
new
Flipmode
album
was
cancelled
and
shelved.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2006:_Aftermath.2FInterscope_era">2006:
Aftermath/Interscope
era</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"
title="Edit
section:
2006:
Aftermath/Interscope
era">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<dl>









<dt>









<i>The
Big
Bang</i>
(2006)








</dt>








</dl>








<p>His
seventh
studio
album,
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Big_Bang_(Busta_Rhymes_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Big
Bang
(Busta
Rhymes
album)">The
Big
Bang</a></i>,
became
the
first
#1
album
of
his
career.
The
CD
sold
over
209,000
copies
in
its
first
week
to
earn
the
top
spot
on
the
US
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
also
became
his
highest
charting
album
in
the
UK,
peaking
at
#19.
Some
of
the
album
was
previously
<a
href="/wiki/Internet_leak?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Internet
leak">leaked
online</a>,
and
as
a
result
several
songs
were
left
off
the
album
and
new
ones
added.
<i>The
Big
Bang</i>
features
<a
href="/wiki/Hip_hop_production?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hip
hop
production">production</a>
by
Dr.
Dre
and
<a
href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Swizz
Beatz">Swizz
Beatz</a>,
as
well
as
appearances
by
<a
href="/wiki/Raekwon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Raekwon">Raekwon</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Nas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nas">Nas</a>.
The
album
spawned
the
singles
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Touch_It?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Touch
It">Touch
It</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Love_My_Bitch?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Love
My
Bitch">I
Love
My
Bitch</a>&quot;,
featuring
<a
href="/wiki/Kelis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kelis">Kelis</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Will.i.am?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a>,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/New_York_Shit?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
Shit">New
York
Shit</a>&quot;,
featuring
Swizz
Beatz
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/In_the_Ghetto_(Busta_Rhymes_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
the
Ghetto
(Busta
Rhymes
song)">In
The
Ghetto</a>&quot;.
Busta
Rhymes
also
had
a
stint
opening
for
<a
href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mariah
Carey">Mariah
Carey</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Mimi_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Adventures
of
Mimi
Tour"
class="mw-redirect">The
Adventures
of
Mimi
Tour</a>.
Also,
he
has
performed
with
<a
href="/wiki/Eminem?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eminem">Eminem</a>
on
&quot;Touch
It
Remix
Part
5&quot;
and
performed
a
verse
on
the
aforementioned
rapper's
song,
&quot;I'll
Hurt
You&quot;.
On
July
17,
2008,
Busta
left
Interscope
and
Aftermath
due
to
a
creative
clash
with
Interscope
head
<a
href="/wiki/Jimmy_Iovine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jimmy
Iovine">Jimmy
Iovine</a>.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2007.E2.80.932009:_Universal_Motown_and_Back_on_My_B.S.">2007–2009:
Universal
Motown
and
<i>Back
on
My
B.S.</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
2007–2009:
Universal
Motown
and
Back
on
My
B.S.">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
2007,
Busta
Rhymes
released
a
song
featuring
<a
href="/wiki/Linkin_Park?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Linkin
Park">Linkin
Park</a>,
titled
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/We_Made_It_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="We
Made
It
(song)"
class="mw-redirect">We
Made
It</a>&quot;.
He
also
made
an
original
song
(&quot;Where's
My
Money&quot;)
for
a
fictional
radio
station
in
the
2008
video
game
<i><a
href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_IV?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grand
Theft
Auto
IV">Grand
Theft
Auto
IV</a></i>.
It
was
later
revealed
that
Busta
inked
a
deal
with
<a
href="/wiki/Universal_Motown?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Universal
Motown"
class="mw-redirect">Universal
Motown</a>,
where
he
released
his
eighth
studio
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Back_on_My_B.S.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Back
on
My
B.S.">Back
on
My
B.S.</a></i>,
on
May
19,
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-universalmotown_16-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-universalmotown-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
debuted
at
#5
on
the
<i>Billboard
200</i>,
selling
56,000
copies,
and
was
his
first
album
to
not
receive
an
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">RIAA
certification</a>,
selling
122,000
copies
to
date.
The
album
was
supported
by
the
singles
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Arab_Money?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Arab
Money">Arab
Money</a>&quot;,
featuring
<a
href="/wiki/Ron_Browz?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ron
Browz">Ron
Browz</a>,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Hustler%27s_Anthem_%2709?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hustler's
Anthem
'09">Hustler's
Anthem
'09</a>&quot;,
featuring
<a
href="/wiki/T-Pain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="T-Pain">T-Pain</a>
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Respect_My_Conglomerate?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Respect
My
Conglomerate">Respect
My
Conglomerate</a>&quot;.
The
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/World_Go_Round?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="World
Go
Round">World
Go
Round</a>&quot;,
featuring
British
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Estelle_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Estelle
(musician)">Estelle</a>,
was
released
in
France
on
April
6,
2009
due
to
the
heavy
rotation
of
a
leaked
version.
The
single
was
released
in
the
UK
on
July
13,
2009.
Busta
Rhymes
also
appeared
on
<a
href="/wiki/Asher_Roth?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Asher
Roth">Asher
Roth</a>'s
debut
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Asleep_in_the_Bread_Aisle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Asleep
in
the
Bread
Aisle">Asleep
in
the
Bread
Aisle</a></i>.</p>








<h4><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Arab_Money_and_Controversy_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates">Arab
Money
and
Controversy
in
the
United
Arab
Emirates</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
Arab
Money
and
Controversy
in
the
United
Arab
Emirates">edit</a>]</span></h4>








<p>Due
to
controversial
content,
the
<a
href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="United
Arab
Emirates">United
Arab
Emirates
(UAE)</a>
has
banned
the
album.
<i>Back
on
My
B.S.</i>
was
released
internationally,
but
because
of
one
song,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Arab_Money?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Arab
Money">Arab
Money</a>&quot;,
it
is
not
available
to
buy
as
a
CD
there
(however,
the
album
can
still
be
purchased
via
<a
href="/wiki/ITunes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ITunes">iTunes</a>).
According
to
the
National
Media
Council,
the
lyrics
were
considered
to
be
offensive
to
Arabs
and
to
<a
href="/wiki/Islam?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Islam">Islam</a>,<sup
class="noprint
Inline-Template"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Please
clarify"><span
title="Why
and
how
may
it
be
considered
to
be
offensive?
(March
2014)">clarification
needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
and
permission
for
distribution
was
therefore
denied.
Some
DJs,
artists
and
fans
have
lambasted
the
track,
saying
it
portrayed
Arabs
in
a
stereotypical
way.
The
first
part
out
of
three
of
the
remix
by
Rhymes
contains
verses
from
the
<a
href="/wiki/Quran?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Quran">Quran</a>.
In
November
2008,
when
&quot;Arab
Money&quot;
was
released
as
a
single,
DJ
Dany
Neville
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Iraqi_people?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Iraqi
people">Iraqi</a>
rapper
The
Narcicyst
responded
by
recording
a
reply.
Busta
later
apologized.
DJs
in
the
country
said
they
had
not
received
an
order
banning
the
record
from
being
spun
in
nightclubs,
and
they
had
mixed
feelings
on
whether
the
record
was
offensive
or
not.<sup
id="cite_ref-thenational.ae_17-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-thenational.ae-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
DJ
Saif
of
<a
href="/wiki/Dubai?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dubai">Dubai</a>
said:</p>








<table
class="cquote"
style="margin:auto;
border-collapse:

auto;">

<td

play

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2010-present:_Cash_Money_Records_and_Extinction_Level_Event_2">2010-present:
Cash
Money
Records
and
<i>Extinction
Level
Event
2</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"
title="Edit
section:
2010-present:
Cash
Money
Records
and
Extinction
Level
Event
2">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
September
2009,
Busta
Rhymes
had
announced
that
he
was
working
on
his
ninth
studio
album,
alongside
Canadian
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Boi-1da?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Boi-1da">Boi-1da</a>,
entitled
<i>The
Chemo</i>.
At
the
time,
he
stated
that
the
project
was
80%
finished.<sup
id="cite_ref-18"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
May
2010,
Busta
Rhymes
had
reportedly
changed
the
title
of
his
ninth
album
for
<i>The
Chemo</i>
to
<i><a
href="/wiki/Extinction_Level_Event_2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Extinction
Level
Event
2"
class="mw-redirect">Extinction
Level
Event
2</a></i>,
making
his
ninth
effort
a
<a
href="/wiki/Sequel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sequel">sequel</a>
to
his
1998
album
<i>Extinction
Level
Event
(Final
World
Front)</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-19"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
an
August
6,
2010
interview
on
Conspiracy
Worldwide
Radio,
American
hip
hop
producer
<a
href="/wiki/DJ_Premier?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="DJ
Premier">DJ
Premier</a>,
said
Busta
Rhymes
received
over
eight
beats
which
he
didn't
want
to
use
but
Premier
hoped
his
next
beat
would
be
chosen
for
inclusion
on
the
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
DJ
Premier's
Live
From
Headqcourterz
radio
show
Premier
confirmed
that
one
of
his
beats
were
to
be
included
in
<i>E.L.E.
2</i>.
In
2010,
Busta
Rhymes
formed
his
new
label
Conglomerate
Records
(With
later
on
having
rosters
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/N.O.R.E.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="N.O.R.E.">N.O.R.E.</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Spliff_Star?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Spliff
Star">Spliff
Star</a>).
He
was
also
featured
on
&quot;C'mon
(Catch
'Em
By
Surprise)&quot;
by
<a
href="/wiki/Ti%C3%ABsto?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ti&euml;sto">Ti&euml;sto</a>
and
Diplo.</p>








<p>In
2011,
Rhymes
recorded
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Look_at_Me_Now_(Chris_Brown_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Look
at
Me
Now
(Chris
Brown
song)">Look
at
Me
Now</a>&quot;
with
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Brown?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Brown">Chris
Brown</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lil
Wayne">Lil
Wayne</a>
on
Brown's
fourth
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/F.A.M.E._(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="F.A.M.E.
(album)">F.A.M.E.</a></i>,
the
song
has
received
favorable
reviews
regarding
Rhymes
guest
verse
on
the
song,
and
is
his
highest
chart
entry
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100">Billboard
Hot
100</a>,
peaking
at
number
six,
while
reaching
number
one
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hot_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Songs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hot
R&amp;B/Hip-Hop
Songs">Hot
R&amp;B/Hip-Hop
Songs</a>
chart,
becoming
his
first
#1
on
that
chart.
On
September
7,
2011,
Rhymes
received
six
nominations
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BET
Hip
Hop
Awards">BET
Hip
Hop
Awards</a>,
held
on
October
11,
2011.</p>








<p>On
May
1,
2011
Rhymes
appeared
on
the
launch
show
for
MNET's
Big
Brother
Africa
6:
Amplified
and
performed
some
of
his
songs.
In
2011,
Busta
Rhymes
performed
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Gathering_of_the_Juggalos?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gathering
of
the
Juggalos">Gathering
of
the
Juggalos</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
Busta
Rhymes
contributed
to
the
2011
<a
href="/wiki/Tech_N9ne?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tech
N9ne">Tech
N9ne</a>
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/All_6%27s_and_7%27s?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
6's
and
7's">All
6's
and
7's</a></i>,
performing
vocals
on
the
single,
&quot;Worldwide
Choppers,&quot;
released
on
May
31.<sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
Canadian
recording
artist
<a
href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Justin
Bieber">Justin
Bieber</a>
featured
Busta
Rhymes
on
a
song
called
&quot;Drummer
Boy&quot;
off
Bieber's
sophomore
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Under_the_Mistletoe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Under
the
Mistletoe">Under
the
Mistletoe</a></i>,
released
on
November
1,
2011.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
November
11,
2011,
a
<a
href="/wiki/Heavy_D?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Heavy
D">Heavy
D</a>
tribute
song
titled
&quot;You
Ain’t
Gotta
Wait
Till
I’m
Gone&quot;
was
leaked.<sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
November
16,
2011,
it
was
announced
that
Busta
Rhymes
signed
to
<a
href="/wiki/Cash_Money_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cash
Money
Records">Cash
Money
Records</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
For
his
debut
single
on
the
Cash
Money
label
and
his
Conglomerate
Records,
he
reunites
with
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Brown?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Brown">Chris
Brown</a>
to
make
the
aggressive
single
known
as
<a
href="/wiki/Why_Stop_Now?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Why
Stop
Now">Why
Stop
Now</a>.
In
2012,
Busta
collaborated
with
<a
href="/wiki/Jodie_Connor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jodie
Connor">Jodie
Connor</a>,
featuring
on
her
single
&quot;Take
You
There&quot;,
but
he
did
not
appear
in
the
music
video.</p>








<p>A
song
with
Twista,
titled
&quot;Can
You
Keep
Up&quot;
was
leaked.
Busta
Rhymes
was
featured
on
<a
href="/wiki/Fat_Joe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fat
Joe">Fat
Joe</a>'s
single
&quot;Pride
&amp;
Joy&quot;
alongside
<a
href="/wiki/Kanye_West?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kanye
West">Kanye
West</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Jadakiss?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jadakiss">Jadakiss</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
ninth
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Year_of_the_Dragon_(Busta_Rhymes_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Year
of
the
Dragon
(Busta
Rhymes
album)">Year
of
the
Dragon</a></i>,
was
released
for
free
on
<a
href="/wiki/Google_Play?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Google
Play">Google
Play</a>
on
August
21,
2012.
The
album
features
guest
appearances
from
<a
href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lil
Wayne">Lil
Wayne</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Rick_Ross?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rick
Ross">Rick
Ross</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Trey_Songz?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trey
Songz">Trey
Songz</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Robin_Thicke?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Robin
Thicke">Robin
Thicke</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Maino?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Maino">Maino</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Gucci_Mane?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gucci
Mane">Gucci
Mane</a>
and
more.
He
also
released
a
music
video
for
the
track
&quot;Doin'
It
Again&quot;
which
features
<a
href="/wiki/Reek_da_Villian?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reek
da
Villian">Reek
da
Villian</a>
which
includes
a
tribute
to
his
manager
that
committed
suicide,
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Lighty?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Lighty">Chris
Lighty</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-27"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>He
also
later
featured
on
YMCMB
label
mate
Shannel
single
&quot;Last
Time&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2011
it
was
announced
that
Universal
Motown
was
going
defunct
making
Rhymes
and
other
arists
move
to
<a
href="/wiki/Universal_Republic_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Universal
Republic
Records">Universal
Republic
Records</a>,
in
mid-2012,
it
was
announced
that
Universal
Republic
Records
was
going
defunct,
making
artists
on
the
roster
move
to
<a
href="/wiki/Republic_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Republic
Records">Republic
Records</a>
making
the
label
revived
itself.<sup
id="cite_ref-29"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
December
21,
members
of
The
Conglomerate
Ent.,
Busta
along
with
J.
Doe
and
Reek
da
Villan
released
a
mixtape
titled
&quot;Catastrophic&quot;,
their
first
collective
effort.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
Busta

collaborated
with
<a

off

A

was

in

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Personal_life">Personal
life</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12"
title="Edit
section:
Personal
life">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Busta
has
three
children
with
his
ex-girlfriend,
Joanne
Wood:
T'Ziah
(born
1993),
T'Khi
(born
1999),
Trillian
(born
2001),
as
well
as
a
daughter,
Mariah
(born
1998),
with
another
ex-girlfriend.</p>








<p>For
a
still-unnamed
<a
href="/wiki/Comedy_Central?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Comedy
Central">Comedy
Central</a>
pilot,
Busta
has
been
prank-called
several
times
by
<a
href="/wiki/Questlove?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Questlove">Questlove</a>
protege
<a
href="/wiki/Danny!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Danny!">Danny!</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Legal_issues">Legal
issues</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13"
title="Edit
section:
Legal
issues">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>On
August
20,
2006,
Busta
Rhymes
was
arrested
and
arraigned
for
charges
of
third-degree
<a
href="/wiki/Assault?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Assault">assault</a>
after
attacking
a
man
who
reportedly
spat
on
his
car
in
New
York
City
on
August
12
after
the
AmsterJam
Music
Festival
on
<a
href="/wiki/Randall%27s_Island?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Randall's
Island"
class="mw-redirect">Randall's
Island</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-37"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
October
24,
2006,
Busta
Rhymes
appeared
at
<a
href="/wiki/Manhattan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>
Criminal
Court
as
the
<a
href="/wiki/District_attorney?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="District
attorney">district
attorney</a>'s
office
attempted
to
amend
previous
charges
against
him
to
include
weapons
possession
for
a
<a
href="/wiki/Machete?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Machete">machete</a>
found
in
his
car.
The
judge
refused
to
add
the
charge
and
adjourned
the
case.<sup
id="cite_ref-NYTimes1_38-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NYTimes1-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-BostonHerald1_39-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BostonHerald1-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
February
20,
2007,
Busta
Rhymes
refused
a
plea
deal
offered
by
the
prosecutor's
office
for
the
assault
of
his
former
driver,
Edward
Hatchett.
The
deal
would
have
entailed
six
months
in
jail
and
<a
href="/wiki/Guilty_plea?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guilty
plea"
class="mw-redirect">pleading
guilty</a>
to
two
assaults,
the
attack
on
Hatchett,
and
the
attack
on
the
former
fan.
The
dispute
with
Hatchett
is
believed
to
have
originated
over
back
pay
Hatchett
felt
he
was
owed.
Manhattan
Criminal
Court
Judge
Becki
Rowe
offered
Busta
another
option,
pleading
guilty
to
third-degree
assault.
The
conditions
of
the
proposed
sentence
would
include
five
days
of
<a
href="/wiki/Community_service?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Community
service">community
service</a>,
two
weeks
of
youth
lectures
and
six
months
of
anger
management
classes,
as
well
as
three
years
of
<a
href="/wiki/Probation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Probation">probation</a>.
On
March
18,
2008
a
judge
in
New
York
City
sentenced
Busta
to
three
years'
probation,
10
days'
<a
href="/wiki/Community_service?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Community
service">community
service</a>,
$1250
in
fines
(plus
court
costs),
and
to
enroll
in
a
drunken
driving
program.<sup
id="cite_ref-BostonHerald1_39-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BostonHerald1-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-CourtTV1_40-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-CourtTV1-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-NYPost1_41-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NYPost1-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-42"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
September
25,
2008,
Busta
Rhymes
was
temporarily
refused
entry
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/United_Kingdom?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="United
Kingdom">United
Kingdom</a>
due
to
&quot;unresolved
convictions&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-43"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
October
14,
2009,
a
Brooklyn
judge
ordered
Busta
Rhymes
to
pay
a
concert
goer
$75,000
in
compensation
for
an
assault
which
occurred
in
2003.<sup
id="cite_ref-44"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

render_ads(false,
window['ad_config_bot']);





function
afc_match()
{








var
count
=
-1;








if(window['ad_config_top'])
{












count
=
window['ad_config_top'];








}









var
countBottom
=
0;








if(window['ad_config_bot'])
{












countBottom
=
window['ad_config_bot'];








}









if(window['backfillParam'])
{




























window['backfillParam']['pl_bmodn']
=
5;
























window['backfillParam']['pl_tnum']
=
count;












window['backfillParam']['pl_bnum']
=
countBottom;








}


































var
_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=Busta_Rhymes&page=1&ac=24&qid=5766CBA37A584F1251520A1D27959651&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();
